40393005b3ba751ae17d260fcde95791|SUN DAILY|ENGLISH|Lisbon, Luxembourg rank Europe's worst for pollution fight|http://www.thesundaily.my/news/1370235|2015-03-31 05:38:45|"BRUSSELS: Lisbon and Luxembourg rank last in a test of how hard European cities are fighting air pollution, while Zurich and Copenhagen come top, an environmental group said Tuesday.\n\nDublin, Glasgow, Madrid and Rome also fared badly in the test of 23 mainly western European cities carried out by Friends of the Earth Germany.\n\n\"Lisbon and Luxembourg finish in the last bottom two places for tackling air pollution in only a half-hearted manner,\" the group said.\n\nThey had done the least to reduce pollution, ban heavy polluters from the roads, introduce clean buses and other forms of public transport, offer economic incentives, promote public transport as well as encourage walking and cycling, it said.\n\nThe gap with the top ranking cities was wide, the group said.\n\n\"Both in Zurich and in the runner-up city, Copenhagen, the number of cars has been substantially reduced and there are restrictions on highly-polluting vehicles such as diesel cars, trucks and construction machines,\" it said.\n\nThe study, based on the US school grading system, gave the Swiss city a \"B plus\" rating while the Danish capital and the Austrian capital Vienna both got Bs.\n\nStockholm got a B minus, Berlin got a C, while Helsinki, London, Paris and the German city of Stuttgart got C minus scores.\n\nAmsterdam in the Netherlands and the Austrian city of Graz were graded D plus. The German city of Duesseldorf, the French city of Lyon, and Brussels were ranked D.\n\nSpanish city Barcelona, Italian industrial hub Milan and the Czech capital Prague all got D minus grades.\n\nDublin, Madrid, Rome and the Scottish city of Glasgow were all given F grades, but were still deemed to be doing slightly better than Portugal's Lisbon and the tiny duchy of Luxembourg.\n\nThe study was backed by the European Environmental Bureau, a coalition of grassroots environmental organisations. \u2013 AFP"|["Lisbon", ",", "Luxembourg", "rank", "Europe", "'", "s", 103f97efbddbaf194f4926aff576f3d1|SUN DAILY|ENGLISH|Models in gas masks highlight Indonesian environmental devastation|http://www.thesundaily.my/news/1370260|2015-03-31 06:24:13|"RANCAEKEK, Indonesia: Wearing gas masks and designer dresses, models paraded down a catwalk against a backdrop of polluted, rubbish-strewn paddy fields in central Indonesia, a colourful condemnation of the fashion industry's role in causing environmental devastation.\n\nThe women marched up and down in black rubber boots on a runway of wooden planks to dance music, brandishing banners that read \"Say no to fashion with a toxic trail\".\n\nThe show, put on by environmental group Greenpeace and local designers, was aimed at highlighting the destruction caused by textile factories, including many producing clothes for global brands, that have for years been spewing industrial waste into the country's waterways. \n\n\"Greenpeace urges the industry to stop polluting the environment with hazardous chemicals,\" said the group's campaigner Ahmad Ashov Birry, who was organising the show. \n\n\"We urge the government to take stern action against the polluters and strengthen regulations related to the management of hazardous chemicals for a toxic-free future.\" \n\nLast week's show took place at Rancaekek, part of the Citarum River Basin on Java island, which is the heart of the Indonesian textile industry. \n\nThe area was named as one of the 10 most polluted places on Earth in 2013 by environmental groups the Blacksmith Institute and Green Cross Switzerland. \n\nThe groups found a wide range of toxins \u2013 including aluminium and manganese \u2013 in the river, which supplies much of the water to the capital Jakarta. \n\nIn Rancaekek alone, more than 1,200 hectares (3,000 acres) of paddy fields have been polluted, according to Greenpeace.\n\nThe show was part of a Greenpeace campaign called \"Detox\", which has been running since 2011 and is aimed at getting well-known brands to ensure that their suppliers do not release hazardous chemicals into the environment. \n\nBig names such as Spain's Zara and Germany's Adidas have committed to the campaign.\n\nRivers and crops have been poisoned by pollution across the vast Indonesian archipelago by a wide range of industries, from manufacturing to mining. \n\nMore than 100 million Indonesians, out of a population of 250 million, have no access to safe water, according to Greenpeace. \u2013 AFP"|["Models", "in", "gas", "masks", "highlight", "Indonesian", "environmental", "devastation"]|["RANCAEKEK", ",", Matchday revenue, which includes ticket sales and hospitality, dropped to 25.9 million from 27.8 million in 2013, while their average Premier League attendances were 50,395 compared to 50,517 the previous season. Revenue declined 1.3 percent to 80.4 billion ringgit.\nPetronas may review its planned $300 billion-ringgit capital expenditure over five years because of falling crude prices, Executive Vice President Wee Yiaw Hin said this month. The spending plan was announced in 2011.\nThe British Columbia government granted environmental permits this week to Petronas\u2019 LNG export terminal and the pipeline linking it to the inland gas fields, according to a statement from the Ministry of Environment. spend their time catching up on the day\u2019s news.\nBut while the commute time has increased, the number of employees in Malaysia looking to remain productive has increased, Regus said, adding these are encouraging signs for Malaysia\u2019s economy, particularly with Vision 2020 on the horizon.\nVijayakumar Tangarasan, Country Manager at Regus Malaysia, said: \u201cInstead of becoming shorter, the global commute has actually increased by a full five minutes each way and now accounts for over an hour a day.\n\"Although the daily commute represents a productivity drain, workers are keeping active on their portable devices and focusing on catching up on some leisure activities such as listening to music while they travel.\n\"During intraday travel, they focus on more professional activities instead.\"\nNevertheless, he said, people would ideally like to be able to work in a professional, discreet environment, near to home or to wherever their business takes them, so that their commuting time is shorter and their productivity can be maximised.\n\"Working closer to home means reducing the daily productivity drain represented by commuting and giving workers an opportunity to improve their work-life balance,\" he said.\nThe survey found the world average commute has increased a full five minutes each way since 2012, with the average one-way commute now taking 32.5 minutes NCB operates the north and south ports in Port Klang. \u00a0.\n\"The acquisition is in line with the initiative of MMC to make further strategic investment in MMC\u2019s core business, the ports and logistics division and to further strengthen MMC\u2019s financial position.\n\u201cIn addition, the acquisition will bode well for MMC which is a key player in the ports industry in Malaysia. It provides a good opportunity for the MMC Group to acquire a strategic stake in an established company in the ports and logistics sector,\u201d the group said in a note to the exchange yesterday.\nThe stake sale is part of MISC's move to divest its non-core businesses and concentrate on its oil and gas related business.\nA business daily news report had speculated that MMC will use NCB as a listed vehicle for the backdoor listing MMC's port assets which, if true, will see MMC stake in NCB rise. NCB is currently controlled by Permodalan Nasional Bhd with a 47.71% stake.\nKenanga Research revised its target price on MMC to RM 2.41 from RM2.81 previously following the proposed stake buy in NCB stating it unsure whether MMC has never indicated intention to buy stakes in port especially at a investment stake level.\n\u201cDespite the group\u2019s earnings delivery, uncertainties persist on the group\u2019s direction on the back of recent news flow which the market has perceived negatively. We believe all these factors could cause an overhang on MMC\u2019s share price in the near to medium term,\u201d said the report. Market sentiment towards MMC could improve with it plan to relist independent power producer (IPP) Malakoff next year.\nOn Tuesday, the sell down took place by as high as 8.2% to intraday low of RM2.24, before rebounding back to closing price of RM2.38. The selling levels were extremely high with 60 million shares transacted in comparison with the three months average daily volume of only three million. MMC shares closed unchanged at RM2.35 yesterday while NCB\u2019s shares increased 13 sen to RM2.65.\nMMC also has an associate stake in Red Sea Gateway Terminal Company Limited which operates a container terminal at Jeddah Islamic Port, Kingdom of Saudi Arabia.\nThe group's independent power producer (IPP) Malakoff has proposed to listing on the second quarter of 2015 involving an offer of 1.52 billion shares or 30.4% of the enlarged share issue and paid up share capital to investors. Of the amount of shares on offer, 521.74 million shares will be sold via an offer for sale while the public issue will consist of one billion new shares with the price to be determined later.\nThe institional offering will involve 1.279 billion IPO shares while retailers will be offered 242.5 million shares. \u00a0Upon listing the paid up capital will consist of RM500 million comprising of five billion offer shares post a corporate exercise that will involve a bonus issues, convertion of 41.79 million redeemable convertible non-cummulativ epreference shares with a par value of 10 sen each and a subdivision of shares.\nMalakoff is now 51% owned by MMC. MMC total cost of investment in the independent power producer Malakoff on April 26, 2006 u pto Oct 31, 2014 is about RM2.047 billion the exchange notice yesterday revealed.\nThe price of the shares will be set through a book building exercise on the institutional price in due course, a MMC filing yesterday revealed. The \u00a0net proceeds from the exercise will be used to repay financing facilities of the MMC group of companies and working capital purposes.\nGross proceeds from the proposed public issue are expected to be used for the redemption of its financing facilities, expansion of business and working capital and other general corporate purposes.\nMalkoff has total generation capacity in Malaysia now stands at 5,346 MW but its Tanjung Bin facility in Johor is expanding capacity by another 1,000MW. Abroad, it has generation capacity of 690MW thus taking its total capacity to 6,036 MW. The group plans to raise it generation capacity to 10,000 MW by 2020.\nMalakoff also undertakes operation and maintenance works on power and water desalination facilities and related assets/contracts across the MENA region. 3c356068473003a53a8f726273500373|MALAYSIAN RESERVE|ENGLISH|FGVH declares RM9.3m net loss for 3Q14 despite record revenue of RM4.3b|http://themalaysianreserve.com/main/news/corporate-malaysia/7886-fgvh-declares-rm93m-net-loss-for-3q14-despite-record-revenue-of-rm43b|2014-11-28 04:33:01|"Felda Global Ventures Holdings Bhd (FGV) declared a RM9.332 million net loss for third quarter ended September 30, 2014 despite declaring a record revenue of RM4.324 billion, the first loss reported since its listing in June 2012.\nThe plantation company attributed the loss to a RM105.54 million of commodity realised and unrealised losses linked to forward and future contracts in FGV's downstream operations.\nTA Securities Holdings Bhd in its research note released yesterday said that the RM105.million unrealized loss included RM52 million incurred by the Canadian crushing business, in addition to a 40.4% quarter on quarter (QoQ) contraction in sugar profit before tax (PBT) and 25.6% QoQ decline in manufacturing, logistics and others (MLO) PBT.\nFGV, in its statement yesterday focused on the 34.3% revenue increase to RM4.32 billion for 3Q14, driven by the consolidation of Felda Holdings Bhd (FHB) and Pontian United Plantations Bhd (PUP).\n\"Not only has the injection of FHB and PUP into FGV had an immediate, positive impact on the group's revenues, it has also allowed FGV to acquire greater alignment and control of the entire plantation value chain and attain higher operational efficiencies and synergies,\" said FGV's Group President and CEO, Datuk Mohd Emir Mavani Abdullah.\nMohd Emir who took the helm of FGV in July 2013 had so far seen FGV revenue ranged from RM2.991 billion in Q213 to the high in 3Q14.\nHe also saw the lowest net profit prior to this where FGV's net profit was RM22.89 million a year ago in Q313.\nMohd Emir said in the statement that FGV has been operating in a challenging global business environment, with crude palm oil (CPO) prices falling to a five-year low during the third quarter, record harvests of US soybeans, and the narrowing price difference between soy oil and palm oil increasing the competitive landscape for the company.\nFGV said it expects the global market for CPO prices to improve in coming quarters, an expectation shared by many leading analysts, which will have a positive impact on its revenue outlook.\nIn addition, FGV said the outlook will be strengthened by the exemption of CPO export duties until the end of 2014, as well as the introduction of the government's B7 biodiesel mandate.\nTA maintained a 'Sell' call on FGV with target price lowered to RM3.53 (RM3.68 previously) post-earnings downgrade.\n\u201cFY14/15/16 earnings forecasts reduced by 28.9%/13.9%/7.8%. This is to take into account the losses in the downstream business and the higher than expected effective tax rate in FY14 (9MFY14: 32.3%),\u201d said TA adding that a bulk of the earnings downgrade is due to downstream business.\nTA opined that despite share price has corrected as much as 13% in the past three months, valuation remains elevated (21 times FY15 price earnings ratio) based on the revised earnings forecasts. \u201cMoreover, the earnings headwinds in the sugar and MLO segments are yet to show signs of turnaround,\u201d said TA.\nFGV ended yesterday's trading down 12 sen to close at RM3.38 per share with 490,900 shares traded. The lowest its price had gone down was in mid October, 2014 where it dipped to RM2.99 per share before closing at RM3.00 per share."|["FGVH", "declares", "RM9", ".", "3m", "net", "loss", "for", with 22 station spanning across 45.1km, including 24.9km underground rail network.\nIn a statement released yesterday, Shahril said the RM9 million consultancy services contract is expected to begin in December 2014.\nHe said phase one of the Makkah Metro is expected to be commissioned by 2019.\n\u201cWe would be responsible to conduct preliminary and detailed design reviews for the project in addition to developing the operations and maintenance specifications and service agreements for the future contractor,\u201d Shahril said.\n\u201cWe would also support and advise the client in the 65a975f1d1e4c3df6cc537e7f18629dc|MALAYSIAN RESERVE|ENGLISH|Najib:M'sian GDP grew 6.1%, highest in Asean|http://themalaysianreserve.com/main/news/corporate-malaysia/7884-najibmsian-gdp-grew-61-highest-in-asean|2014-11-28 04:27:35|"\nAt the Umno General Assembly, Najib also announced that he has made the decision to maintain the Sedition Act 1948, with improvements to include 2 special provisions to further strengthen the Act. (Pic by Husseon Shaharuddin/TMR)\n\nPrime Minister Datuk Seri Najib Razak, while presenting the country's report card during the United Malays National Organisation (UMNO) general assembly in Kuala Lumpur yesterday, said Malaysia's gross domestic product (GDP) most recently grew 6.1%, the highest in Asean.\nNajib, who is also UMNO president, said Malaysia's has been able to achieve this on the back of an encouraging growth across all sectors despite the uncertainties in the global economic environment.\n\u201cIn fact, for nearly six decades now, we have achieved some amazing economic performances and records that we are able to be proud of on the back of a stable and systematic policies,\u201d he said.\nOn the other hand, Najib also said that the country recorded a historical high for foreign direct investment totalling RM38.7 billion in 2013. During July 2014, Bursa Malaysia Index has also recorded its highest level at 1,892 points. The country also continues its position as the world's largest sukuk market, he said.\nHe also quoted a World Bank Group's \u201cDoing Business 2015 Report\u201d as saying that Malaysia was ranked 18th out of 189 countries globally and CNN Travel Report as saying Kuala Lumpur ranked as the fourth most popular city for shopping in 2013 after New York, Tokyo and London.\nBesides that, Najib has also announced that he has made the decision after listening to and considering the views of the public, including UMNO members, to maintain the Sedition Act 1948 with improvements to include two special provisions to further strengthen the Act.\nHe said the special provisions aimed to preserve the sanctity of Islam and other religions as well as prosecute those who called for the separation of Sabah and Sarawak from Malaysia.\n\u201cThis is our aspiration and I believe others in the Barisan Nasional leadership are with us, so enforcement must be fair for us to create a more peaceful, stable and harmonious country,\u201d he said.\nSuggestions to repeal the Sedition Act 1948 was first made in July 2012, and to be replaced by a new act to be known as the National Harmony Act.\nThe proposal initially aimed to look for a mechanism that would ensure the best continuity between the need to ensure freedom of speech and the need to tackle the complexity of the plural society in Malaysia.\nHowever, the suggestion was met with opposition from various quarters who gave critical views calling for the act to be retained to tackle issues that could cause racial and religious bccc19c91995856fdee7619a50b6e53d|SUN DAILY|ENGLISH|Anti-terror law tabled|http://www.thesundaily.my/news/1369846|2015-03-30 12:49:28|"KUALA LUMPUR: The new anti-terrorism law, tabled in the Dewan Rakyat today, not only gives police the power to arrest without a warrant but also prohibits judicial reviews on orders for detention without trial, which can be extended indefinitely.\n\nThe Prevention of Terrorism 2015 Bill was tabled by Home Minister Datuk Seri Ahmad Zahid Hamidi (pix).\n\nIt states that judicial reviews can only be made on procedural matters and that the detention orders can be extended from \"time to time for further periods\", for a period not exceeding two years at a time.\n\n\"There shall be no judicial review in any court, and no court shall have or exercise any jurisdiction in respect of, any act done or decision made by the Board in the exercise of its discretionary power in accordance with this Act, except in regard to any question on compliance with any procedural requirement in this Act governing such act or decision,\" the bill states.\n\nThe board refers to the Prevention of Anti-Terrorism Board, consisting of a maximum of eight members appointed by the Yang di-Pertuan Agong, which must be established if the new law is passed.\n\nSimilar to the abolished Internal Security Act (ISA), police have the power to arrest anyone without a warrant if there is reason to believe that grounds exist for the person to be detained and brought before a special inquiry.\n\nThe law allows for a detention in custody for 21 days on a magistrate's order and a further 38 if the investigations show it is necessary.\n\n\"Any person arrested must be produced before a magistrate, who on production of a written statement on holding the inquiry, must either order his detention in custody for a period of 21 days or direct his release if no such statement is produced,\" the bill states.\n\nOther highlights:\n* No person shall be arrested solely for his political belief or political activity.\n* Inquiry officer to be appointed by the minister but no police officer shall be an inquiry officer.\n\nAhmad Zahid had said previously that the law is specifically to address the threats of Islamic State (IS).\n\nThis bill is in line with the White Paper on addressing IS threats in Parliament last November, tabled by Prime Minister Datuk Seri Najib Abdul Razak.\n\nThe enactment of this law will also see other laws like the Security Offences (Special Measures) Act 2012, Prevention of Crime Act 1959 and the Penal Code being amended."|["Anti", "-", "terror", "law", "tabled"]|["KUALA", "LUMPUR", ":", "The", "new", "anti", "-", "terrorism", "law", ",", "tabled", "in", "the", "Dewan", "Rakyat", "today", ",", "not", "only", 936356dd127fa3e73614cca3bd1833fd|SUN DAILY|ENGLISH|Najib: Pan Borneo Highway to be toll-free|http://www.thesundaily.my/news/1370295|2015-03-31 06:44:12|"BINTULU: The Pan Borneo Highway will be toll-free, Prime Minister Datuk Seri Najib Abdul Razak said today. He said the highway was the main artery connecting Sarawak and Sabah and there were no alternative routes between the two states. \n\nThis was unlike the case in peninsular Malaysia where the North-South Expressway was the main link and there were many alternative routes, he said when launching the first phase of the highway, the Pan Borneo Sarawak, that costs RM13 billion. \n\nNajib said toll was imposed on the North-South Expressway in peninsular Malaysia but the people could choose to travel on the toll-free alternative routes. \n\nHe also said that the subsequent phases of the Pan Borneo Highway would be built also this year, with the next launch expected to take place in September.\n\nNajib said that upon completion, the highway would not only improve the infrastructure of Sarawak but also open up economic opportunities for the people in the state. \n\nThe project would bring long-term benefits for the people of the state and was not a mega project that drained public funds, he said. \n\nThe whole Pan Borneo Highway, to be built at a cost of RM27 billion, involves the construction and upgrading of 1,663 kilometres of road in Sarawak and Sabah, with 936km in Sarawak and 727km in Sabah. \n\nThe current project in Sarawak involves the construction of 919 kilometres of a single carriageway from Tanjung Datu to Sematan and a dual carriageway from Sematan to Merapok. \n\nThe construction officially begins today in Sarawak, with the first phase of 43 kilometres from Nyabau to Bakun expected to be completed at the end of 2017, followed by the Tanjung Datu-Sematan-Miri-Limbang-Lawas stretch that is expected to be ready in the middle of 2023. \n\nSarawak Chief Minister Tan Sri Adenan Satem, who also spoke at the launch, said negotiations with the highway concessionaires in Kuching, Sibu and Miri had yet to reach a decision on whether to reduce or abolish toll. \n\n\"If possible, we want to abolish the toll, but this has yet to be decided. We want to reduce the burden on the road users who have to pay road tax, and reduce the cost of living now that the Goods and Services Tax (GST) is to be imposed (from tomorrow),\" he said. \n\nAdenan said the federal government decision to waive toll on the Pan Borneo Highway was apt because the road was an important link for the people of Sarawak for economic and social reasons. \n\nHe also said that the construction of the highway reflected the strong commitment of the federal government in fulfilling the pledges made in the manifesto of the 13th General Election. \n\nSarawak Deputy Chief Minister Tan Sri Alfred Jabu; federal and state ministers; Chief Secretary to the Government Tan Sri Dr Ali Hamsa; heads of departments and community leaders also attended the launch. \u2013
